window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Dr._Dre';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"dr.,_,dre,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Andre
Romelle
Young</b>
(born
February
18,
1965),
known
by
his
<a
href="/wiki/Stage_name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stage
name">stage
name</a>
<b>Dr.
Dre</b>,
is
an
American
record
producer,
<a
href="/wiki/Rapper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rapper"
class="mw-redirect">rapper</a>
and
entrepreneur.
He
is
the
founder
and
current
CEO
of
<a
href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Aftermath
Entertainment">Aftermath
Entertainment</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Beats_Electronics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beats
Electronics">Beats
Electronics</a>.
Dre
was
previously
the
co-owner
of,
and
an
artist
on,
<a
href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Death
Row
Records">Death
Row
Records</a>.
He
has
produced
albums
for
and
overseen
the
careers
of
many
rappers,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Snoop
Dogg">Snoop
Dogg</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Eminem?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eminem">Eminem</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Xzibit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/50_Cent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50
Cent">50
Cent</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Game_(rapper)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Game
(rapper)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Game</a>
and
more
recently
<a
href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kendrick
Lamar">Kendrick
Lamar</a>.
He
is
credited
as
a
key
figure
in
the
popularization
of
<a
href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="West
Coast
hip
hop">West
Coast</a>
<a
href="/wiki/G-funk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="G-funk">G-funk</a>,
a
style
of
rap
music
characterized
as
synthesizer-based
with
slow,
heavy
beats.
In
2011,
Dr.
Dre
was
ranked
as
the
third
richest
figure
in
the
American
hip
hop
scene
by
<a
href="/wiki/Forbes_magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Forbes
magazine"
class="mw-redirect">Forbes</a>
with
a
net
worth
of
$250
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Dre
began
his
career
as
a
member
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/World_Class_Wreckin%27_Cru?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru">World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru</a>
and
later
found
fame
with
the
influential
<a
href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gangsta
rap">gangsta
rap</a>
group
<a
href="/wiki/N.W.A?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Eazy-E?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ice_Cube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ice
Cube">Ice
Cube</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/MC_Ren?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MC
Ren">MC
Ren</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Yella?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Yella">DJ
Yella</a>,
which
popularized
the
use
of
explicit
lyrics
in
rap
to
detail
the
violence
of
street
life.
His
1992
solo
debut
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Chronic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chronic">The
Chronic</a></i>,
released
under
Death
Row
Records,
led
him
to
become
one
of
the
best-selling
American
performing
artists
of
1993
and
to
win
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
Me
Ride">Let
Me
Ride</a>&quot;.
That
same
year
he
produced
Death
Row
labelmate
<a
href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Snoop
Dogg">Snoop
Dogg</a>'s
quadruple
platinum
debut
<i><a
href="/wiki/Doggystyle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i>.</p>








<p>In
1996,
he
left
Death
Row
to
establish
his
own
label,
Aftermath
Entertainment.
He
produced
a
compilation
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dr._Dre_Presents_the_Aftermath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dr.
Dre
Presents
the
Aftermath">Dr.
Dre
Presents
the
Aftermath</a></i>
in
1996,
and
released
a
solo
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/2001_(Dr._Dre_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2001
(Dr.
Dre
album)">2001</a></i>
in
1999,
for
which
he
won
the
Grammy
producer's
award.
During
the
2000s,
he
focused
on
production
for
other
artists,
while
occasionally
contributing
vocals
to
songs.
Dr.
Dre
signed
<a
href="/wiki/Eminem?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eminem">Eminem</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/50_Cent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50
Cent">50
Cent</a>
to
his
record
label
in
1998
and
2003
respectively,
while
contributing
production
on
their
albums.
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
has
also
had
acting
roles
in
movies
such
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Set_It_Off?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Set
It
Off">Set
It
Off</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Wash_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Wash
(film)">The
Wash</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Training_Day?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Training
Day">Training
Day</a></i>.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
ranked
Dre
at
56
on
their
list
of
&quot;100
Greatest
Artists
of
All-Time&quot;.</p>








<div
style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Andr&eacute;
Romelle
Young
was
born
in
<a
href="/wiki/Compton,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Compton,
California">Compton,
California</a>
on
February
18,
1965.
He
was
the
first
child
of
Theodore
and
Verna
Young.
Andr&eacute;'s
middle
name,
Romelle,
is
derived
from
his
father's
amateur
<a
href="/wiki/R%26B?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R&amp;B"
class="mw-redirect">R&amp;B</a>
singing
group,
The
Romells.
Married
in
1964,
Andr&eacute;'s
parents
separated
in
1968
and
divorced
in
1972.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Verna
later
married
Curtis
Crayon.
They
had
three
children
together,
two
sons
named
Jerome
and
Tyree
(both
deceased)<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
daughter
Shameka.<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1976,
Young
began
attending
Vanguard
Junior
High
School
in
Compton,
but
due
to
<a
href="/wiki/Gang?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gang">gang</a>
violence,
he
transferred
to
the
safer
suburban
Roosevelt
Junior
High
School.<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Verna
later
married
Warren
Griffin,
whom
she
met
at
her
new
job
in
Long
Beach,<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
added
three
stepsisters
and
one
stepbrother
to
the
family.
His
stepbrother
Warren
Griffin
III,
would
eventually
become
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Warren_G?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warren
G">Warren
G</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Young
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Centennial_High_School_(Compton,_California)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Centennial
High
School
(Compton,
California)">Centennial
High
School</a>
in
Compton
during
his
freshman
year
in
1979,
but
transferred
to
<a
href="/wiki/John_C._Fremont_High_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
C.
Fremont
High
School">Fremont
High
School</a>
due
to
poor
grades.
Young
attempted
to
enroll
in
an
apprenticeship
program
at
<a
href="/wiki/Northrop_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Northrop
Corporation">Northrop
Aviation
Company</a>,
but
poor
grades
at
school
made
him
ineligible.
Thereafter,
he
focused
on
his
social
life
and
entertainment
for
the
remainder
of
his
high
school
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Young
fathered
a
son,
Curtis,
born
December
15,
1981,
with
Lisa
Johnson.
Curtis
Young
was
brought
up
by
his
mother
and
first
met
his
father
20
years
later,
when
Curtis
became
rapper
Hood
Surgeon.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1984.E2.80.9385:_World_Class_Wreckin.27_Cru">1984â€“85:
World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1984â€“85:
World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Inspired
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grandmaster_Flash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grandmaster
Flash">Grandmaster
Flash</a>
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Grandmaster_Flash_on_the_Wheels_of_Steel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Adventures
of
Grandmaster
Flash
on
the
Wheels
of
Steel">The
Adventures
of
Grandmaster
Flash
on
the
Wheels
of
Steel</a>&quot;,
he
often
attended
a
club
called
The
Eve
After
Dark
to
watch
many
DJs
and
rappers
performing
live.
He
subsequently
became
a
DJ
in
the
club,
initially
under
the
name
&quot;Dr.
J&quot;,
based
on
the
nickname
of
<a
href="/wiki/Julius_Erving?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Julius
Erving">Julius
Erving</a>,
his
favorite
basketball
player.
At
the
club,
he
met
aspiring
rapper
Antoine
Carraby,
later
to
become
member
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Yella?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Yella">DJ
Yella</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/N.W.A?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Soon
afterwards
he
adopted
the
moniker
Dr.&nbsp;Dre,
a
mix
of
previous
alias
Dr.
J
and
his
first
name,
referring
to
himself
as
the
&quot;Master
of
Mixology&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
joined
the
musical
group
<a
href="/wiki/World_Class_Wreckin%27_Cru?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru">World
Class
Wreckin'
Cru</a>
under
the
independent
<a
href="/wiki/Kru-Cut_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kru-Cut
Records">Kru-Cut
Records</a>
in
1984.
The
group
would
become
stars
of
the
electro-hop
scene
that
dominated
early
1980s
<a
href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="West
Coast
hip
hop">West
Coast
hip
hop</a>,
and
their
first
hit
&quot;Surgery&quot;
would
prominently
feature
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
on
the
turntables
and
sell
50,000&nbsp;copies
within
the
Compton
area.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
and
DJ
Yella
also
performed
mixes
for
local
radio
station
<a
href="/wiki/KDAY?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KDAY">KDAY</a>,
boosting
ratings
for
its
afternoon
rush-hour
show
<i>The
Traffic
Jam</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.
Dre's
earliest
recordings
were
released
in
1994
on
a
compilation
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Concrete_Roots?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concrete
Roots">Concrete
Roots</a></i>.
Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine
of
the
website
<i>Allmusic</i>
described
the
compiled
music,
released
&quot;several
years
before
Dre
developed
a
distinctive
style&quot;,
as
&quot;surprisingly
generic
and
unengaging&quot;
and
&quot;for
dedicated
fans
only&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>His
frequent
absences
from
school
jeopardized
his
position
as
a
diver
on
his
school's
swim
team.
After
high
school,
he
attended
Chester
Adult
School
in
Compton
following
his
mother's
demands
for
him
to
get
a
job
or
continue
his
education.
After
brief
attendance
at
a
radio
broadcasting
school,
he
relocated
to
the
residence
of
his
father
and
residence
of
his
grandparents
before
returning
to
his
mother's
house.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
dropped
out
of
Chester
to
focus
on
performing
at
the
Eve's
After
Dark
nightclub.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1986.E2.80.9391:_N.W.A_and_Ruthless_Records">1986â€“91:
N.W.A
and
Ruthless
Records</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1986â€“91:
N.W.A
and
Ruthless
Records">edit</a>]</span></h3>

class="mbox-small-left"
style="border:1px
solid
#aaa;
background-color:#f9f9f9;
float:left;">









<tbody>









<tr>











<td
class="mbox-image">












<div
class="center">













<div
class="floatnone">













<img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png"

<p>In
1986,
Dr.
Dre
met
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Ice_Cube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ice
Cube">Ice
Cube</a>,
who
collaborated
with
Dr.
Dre
to
record
songs
for
<a
href="/wiki/Ruthless_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ruthless
Records">Ruthless
Records</a>,
a
rap
record
label
run
by
local
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Eazy-E?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a>.
<a
href="/wiki/N.W.A?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="N.W.A">N.W.A</a>
and
fellow
West
Coast
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Ice-T?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ice-T">Ice-T</a>
are
widely
credited
as
seminal
artists
of
the
gangsta
rap
genre,
a
profanity-heavy
subgenre
of
hip
hop,
replete
with
gritty
depictions
of
urban
crime
and
gang
lifestyle.
Not
feeling
constricted
to
racially
charged
political
issues
pioneered
by
rap
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Public_Enemy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
Enemy
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">Public
Enemy</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Boogie_Down_Productions?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boogie
Down
Productions">Boogie
Down
Productions</a>,
N.W.A
favored
themes
and
uncompromising
lyrics,
offering
stark
descriptions
of
violent,
inner-city
streets.
Propelled
by
the
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fuck_tha_Police?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fuck
tha
Police">Fuck
tha
Police</a>&quot;,
the
group's
first
full
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Straight_Outta_Compton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Straight
Outta
Compton">Straight
Outta
Compton</a></i>
became
a
major
success,
despite
an
almost
complete
absence
of
radio
airplay
or
major
concert
tours.
The
<a
href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Federal
Bureau
of
Investigation">Federal
Bureau
of
Investigation</a>
sent
Ruthless
Records
a
warning
letter
in
response
to
the
song's
content.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
Ice
Cube
left
N.W.A
in
1989
over
financial
disputes,
Dr.
Dre
produced
and
performed
for
much
of
the
group's
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Efil4zaggin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Efil4zaggin"
class="mw-redirect">Efil4zaggin</a></i>.
He
also
produced
tracks
for
a
number
of
other
rap
acts
on
Ruthless
Records,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Above_the_Law_(group)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Above
the
Law
(group)">Above
the
Law</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_D.O.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
D.O.C.">The
D.O.C.</a>
for
his
1989
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/No_One_Can_Do_It_Better?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
One
Can
Do
It
Better">No
One
Can
Do
It
Better</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-doc_formula_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-doc_formula-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1991,
at
a
music
industry
party
in
Hollywood,
he
assaulted
television
host
<a
href="/wiki/Dee_Barnes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dee
Barnes">Dee
Barnes</a>
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fox
Broadcasting
Company">Fox</a>
television
program
<i>Pump
it
Up</i>,
because
he
felt
dissatisfied
with
her
news
report
about
the
feud
between
the
remaining
N.W.A
members
and
Ice
Cube.
Subsequently,
Dr.
Dre
was
fined
$2,500
and
given
two
years'
probation
and
240
hours
of
community
service,
as
well
as
a
spot
on
an
anti-violence
<a
href="/wiki/Public_service_announcement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Public
service
announcement">public
service
announcement</a>
on
television.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>After
a
dispute
with
Eazy-E,
Dre
left
the
group
at
the
peak
of
its
popularity
in
1991
under
the
advice
of
friend,
and
N.W.A
lyricist,
<a
href="/wiki/The_D.O.C.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
D.O.C.">The
D.O.C.</a>
and
his
bodyguard
at
the
time,
<a
href="/wiki/Suge_Knight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suge
Knight">Suge
Knight</a>.
Knight,
a
notorious
strongman
and
intimidator,
was
able
to
have
Eazy-E
release
Young
from
his
contract
and,
using
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
as
his
flagship
artist,
founded
<a
href="/wiki/Death_Row_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Death
Row
Records">Death
Row
Records</a>.
In
1992
Young
released
his
first
single,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Deep_Cover_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Cover
(song)">title
track</a>
to
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Deep_Cover?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Cover">Deep
Cover</a></i>,
a
collaboration
with
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Snoop
Dogg">Snoop
Dogg</a>,
whom
he
met
through
Warren
G.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
debut
solo
album
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Chronic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chronic">The
Chronic</a></i>,
released
under
Death
Row
Records.
Young
ushered
in
a
new
style
of
rap,
both
in
terms
of
musical
style
and
lyrical
content.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
the
strength
of
singles
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Nuthin%27_but_a_%22G%22_Thang?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nuthin'
but
a
&quot;G&quot;
Thang"
class="mw-redirect">Nuthin'
but
a
'G'
Thang</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
Me
Ride">Let
Me
Ride</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fuck_wit_Dre_Day_(and_Everybody%27s_Celebratin%27)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fuck
wit
Dre
Day
(and
Everybody's
Celebratin')"
class="mw-redirect">Fuck
wit
Dre
Day
(and
Everybody's
Celebratin')</a>&quot;
(known
as
&quot;Dre
Day&quot;
for
radio
and
television
play),
all
of
which
featured
Snoop
Dogg
as
guest
vocalist,
<i>The
Chronic</i>
became
a
cultural
phenomenon,
its
<a
href="/wiki/G-funk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="G-funk">G-funk</a>
sound
dominating
much
of
hip
hop
music
for
the
early
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1993
the
<a
href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Recording
Industry
Association
of
America">Recording
Industry
Association
of
America</a>
(RIAA)
certified
the
album
triple
platinum,<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
also
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rap
Solo
Performance">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rap
Solo
Performance</a>
for
his
performance
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
Me
Ride">Let
Me
Ride</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
that
year,
<i>Billboard</i>
magazine
also
ranked
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
as
the
eighth
best-selling
musical
artist,
<i>The
Chronic</i>
as
the
sixth
best-selling
album,
and
&quot;Nuthin'
but
a
'G'
Thang&quot;
as
the
11th
best-selling
single.<sup
id="cite_ref-pop_life_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-pop_life-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Besides
working
on
his
own
material,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
produced
Snoop
Dogg's
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Doggystyle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i>,
which
became
the
first
debut
album
for
an
artist
to
debut
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
album
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1994
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
produced
some
songs
on
the
soundtracks
to
the
films
<i><a
href="/wiki/Above_the_Rim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Above
the
Rim">Above
the
Rim</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Murder_Was_the_Case?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Murder
Was
the
Case">Murder
Was
the
Case</a></i>.
He
collaborated
with
fellow
N.W.A
member
Ice
Cube
for
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Natural_Born_Killaz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Natural
Born
Killaz">Natural
Born
Killaz</a>&quot;
in
1995.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Friday_(1995_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Friday
(1995
film)">Friday</a></i>,
Dre
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Keep_Their_Heads_Ringin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
Their
Heads
Ringin'">Keep
Their
Heads
Ringin'</a>&quot;,
which
reached
number
ten
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
and
number
1
on
the
Hot
Rap
Singles
(now
Hot
Rap
Tracks)
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-dr-dre-sin_28-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-dr-dre-sin-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1995,
Death
Row
Records
signed
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tupac
Shakur">2Pac</a>,
and
began
to
position
him
as
their
major
star:
he
collaborated
with
Dr.
Dre
on
the
commercially
successful
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/California_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="California
Love">California
Love</a>&quot;,
which
became
both
artists'
first
song
to
top
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
in
early
1996
Young
left
the
label
amidst
a
contract
dispute
and
growing
concerns
that
label
boss
<a
href="/wiki/Suge_Knight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suge
Knight">Suge
Knight</a>
was
corrupt,
financially
dishonest
and
out
of
control.
Later
that
year,
he
formed
his
own
label,
Aftermath
Entertainment,
under
the
distribution
label
for
Death
Row
Records,
<a
href="/wiki/Interscope_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Interscope
Records">Interscope
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Subsequently,
Death
Row
Records
suffered
poor
sales
by
1997,
especially
following
the
death
of
2Pac
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Racket_(crime)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Racket
(crime)">racketeering</a>
charges
brought
against
Knight.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Dr.
Dre
also
appeared
on
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/No_Diggity?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Diggity">No
Diggity</a>&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhythm
and
blues">R&amp;B</a>
group
<a
href="/wiki/Blackstreet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blackstreet">Blackstreet</a>
in
1996:
it
too
was
a
sales
success,
topping
the
Hot
100
for
four
consecutive
weeks,
and
later
won
the
award
for
Best
R&amp;B
Vocal
by
a
Duo
or
Group
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/1997_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1997
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">1997
Grammy
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
hearing
it
for
the
first
time,
several
of
Dr.
Dre's
former
Death
Row
colleagues,
including
2Pac,
recorded
and
attempted
to
release
a
song
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Toss_It_Up?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toss
It
Up">Toss
It
Up</a>&quot;,
containing
numerous
insults
aimed
at
Dr.
Dre
and
using
a
deliberately
similar
instrumental
to
&quot;No
Diggity&quot;,
but
were
forced
to
replace
the
production
after
Blackstreet
issued
the
label
with
a
<a
href="/wiki/Cease_and_desist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cease
and
desist">cease
and
desist</a>
order
stopping
them
from
distributing
the
song.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"

<p>The
<i><a

Presents

by

<a

title="Aftermath
Entertainment">Aftermath
Entertainment</a>
artists,
and
a

&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Been_There,_Done_That?qsrc=3044"

Done

Done

<a

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite

id="cite_ref-RIAA_24-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
the

was

id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

performed
&quot;Been
There,
Done
That&quot;
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday

Live</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

Dre
produced
several
tracks
on
<a
href="/wiki/The_Firm_(hip_hop_group)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The

(hip

group)">The

<i><a

title="The
Album
(The
Firm
album)">The
Album</a></i>;
it
was

with

negative
reviews
from
critics.
Rumors

to

that
Aftermath
was
facing

id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Aftermath
Entertainment
also

a
<a
href="/wiki/Trademark_infringement?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

lawsuit
by

id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="First

Knock
Out">First

Out</a></i>,

Dre
was

to

to

recordings.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The

sign

to

â€“

â€“

<p>Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
second
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/2001_(Dr._Dre_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2001
(Dr.
Dre
album)">2001</a></i>,
released
on
November
16,
1999,
was
considered
an
ostentatious
return
to
his
gangsta
rap
roots.<sup
id="cite_ref-2001_amg_41-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2001_amg-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
initially
titled
<i>The
Chronic
2000</i>
to
imply
being
a
sequel
to
his
debut
solo
effort
<i>The
Chronic</i>
but
was
re-titled
<i>2001</i>
after
Death
Row
Records
released
an
unrelated
compilation
album
with
the
title
<i>Chronic
2000:
Still
Smokin</i>
in
May
1999.
Other
tentative
titles
included
<i>The
Chronic
2001</i>
and
<i>Dr.&nbsp;Dre</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-changes_2001_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-changes_2001-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
featured
numerous
collaborators,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Devin_the_Dude?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devin
the
Dude">Devin
the
Dude</a>,
Hittman,
Snoop
Dogg,
<a
href="/wiki/Xzibit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nate_Dogg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nate
Dogg">Nate
Dogg</a>
and
Eminem.
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>
of
the
website
<a
href="/wiki/Allmusic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allmusic"
class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>
described
the
sound
of
the
album
as
&quot;adding
ominous
<a
href="/wiki/Strings_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strings
(music)"
class="mw-redirect">strings</a>,
soulful
vocals,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Reggae?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reggae">reggae</a>&quot;
to
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
style.<sup
id="cite_ref-2001_amg_41-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2001_amg-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
highly
successful,
charting
at
number
two
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
charts<sup
id="cite_ref-drecharts_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-drecharts-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
has
since
been
certified
six
times
platinum,<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_24-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
validating
a
recurring
theme
on
the
album:
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
still
a
force
to
be
reckoned
with,
despite
the
lack
of
major
releases
in
the
previous
few
years.
The
album
included
popular
hit
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Still_D.R.E.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Still
D.R.E.">Still
D.R.E.</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Forgot_About_Dre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Forgot
About
Dre">Forgot
About
Dre</a>&quot;,
both
of
which
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
performed
on
NBC's
<i>Saturday
Night
Live</i>
on
October
23,
1999.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Producer
of
the
Year,
Non-Classical"
class="mw-redirect">Producer
of
the
Year,
Non-Classical</a>
in
2000,<sup
id="cite_ref-Allmusic_19-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Allmusic-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
joined
the
Up
in
Smoke
Tour
with
fellow
rappers
Eminem,
Snoop
Dogg,
and
Ice
Cube
that
year
as
well.<sup
id="cite_ref-up_in_smoke_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-up_in_smoke-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
the
course
of
<i>2001'</i>s
popularity,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
involved
in
several
lawsuits.
<a
href="/wiki/Lucasfilm_Ltd.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lucasfilm
Ltd."
class="mw-redirect">Lucasfilm
Ltd.</a>,
the
film
company
behind
the
<a
href="/wiki/Star_Wars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Star
Wars">Star
Wars
film
franchise</a>,
sued
him
over
the
use
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/THX?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="THX">THX</a>-trademarked
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Deep_Note?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Note">Deep
Note</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-lucasfilm_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lucasfilm-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Fatback
Band
also
sued
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
over
alleged
infringement
regarding
its
song
&quot;Backstrokin'&quot;
in
his
song
&quot;Let's
Get
High&quot;
from
the
<i>2001</i>
album;
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
ordered
to
pay
$1.5&nbsp;million
to
the
band
in
2003.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
online
music
file-sharing
company
<a
href="/wiki/Napster?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Napster">Napster</a>
also
settled
a
lawsuit
with
him
and
heavy
metal
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/Metallica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metallica">Metallica</a>
in
the
summer
of
2001,
agreeing
to
block
access
to
certain
files
that
artists
do
not
want
to
have
shared
on
the
network.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2001.E2.80.9308:_Focus_on_production">2001â€“08:
Focus
on
production</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
2001â€“08:
Focus
on

<p>Following
the
success
of
<i>2001</i>,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
focused
on
producing
songs
and
albums
for
other
artists.
He
co-produced
six
tracks
on
Eminemâ€™s
landmark
<i><a
href="/wiki/Marshall_Mathers_LP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marshall
Mathers
LP"
class="mw-redirect">Marshall
Mathers
LP</a></i>,
including
the
Grammy-winning
lead

â€œ<a

<p>Another

hit
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
in
the

of
2002,
when
<a

<a

<p>Another

a

between
Aftermath,
Eminem's

label
<a
href="/wiki/Shady_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shady
Records">Shady
Records</a>
and
Interscope.<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
Eminem's
fourth
album
since
joining
Aftermath,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Encore_(Eminem_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Encore
(Eminem
album)">Encore</a></i>,
again
saw
Dre
taking

the

and

In

<i>Vibe</i>
magazine

Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was

In

<a
href="/wiki/Young_Buck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Young
Buck">Young
Buck</a>
stabbed
the
man.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
Johnson
claimed
that

Knight,

of

Dre
in

before
he
received
his

Award.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
Knight
immediately
went
on
<a
href="/wiki/CBS?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CBS">CBS</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_(CBS_TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Late
Late
Show
(CBS
TV
series)">The
Late
Late
Show</a></i>
to
deny
involvement
and
insisted
that
he
supported
Dr.
Dre
and
wanted
Johnson
charged.<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
In

2005,

was

to
a

<p><i>Detox</i>
is
slated
to
be
Dr.
Dre's
final
studio
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard_2007_72-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard_2007-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
Work
for
the
upcoming
album
dates
back
to
2001,<sup
id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre.27s_Final_Album_Will_Be_Hip-Hop_Musical_73-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre.27s_Final_Album_Will_Be_Hip-Hop_Musical-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
where
its
first
version
was
called
&quot;the
most
advanced
rap
album
ever,&quot;
by
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Storch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Storch">Scott
Storch</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Dr._Dre.27s_Detox_.27The_Most_Advanced_Rap_Album_Ever.2C.27_Co-Producer_Says_74-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Dr._Dre.27s_Detox_.27The_Most_Advanced_Rap_Album_Ever.2C.27_Co-Producer_Says-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup>
Later
in
that
year,
he
decided
to
stop
working
on
the
album
to
focus
on
producing
for
other
artists,
but
then
changed
his
mind;
the
album
had
initially
been
set
for
a
fall
2005
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup>
Producers
confirmed
to
work
on
the
album
include
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Khalil?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Khalil">DJ
Khalil</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nottz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nottz">Nottz</a>,
Bernard
&quot;Focus&quot;
Edwards
Jr.,<sup
id="cite_ref-focus_76-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-focus-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Hi-Tek?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hi-Tek">Hi-Tek</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/J.R._Rotem?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J.R.
Rotem">J.R.
Rotem</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/RZA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RZA"
class="mw-redirect">RZA</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Jay-Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Warren_G?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warren
G">Warren
G</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Boi-1da?qsrc=3044"

title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a>.<sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Snoop
Dogg">Snoop
Dogg</a>
claimed
that
<i>Detox</i>
was
finished,
according
to
a
June
2008
report
by
<i>Rolling

magazine.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
another
delay
based
on
producing
other

work,
<i>Detox</i>
was
then
scheduled
for
a
2010
release,
coming
after
50

<i><a
href="/wiki/Before_I_Self_Destruct?qsrc=3044"

title="Before

Self
Destruct">Before

Self
Destruct</a></i>
and
Eminem's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Relapse_(Eminem_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Relapse
(Eminem
album)">Relapse</a></i>,
an
album
for
which
Dr.
Dre
handled
the
bulk
of
production
duties.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
a
<a
href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dr
Pepper">Dr
Pepper</a>
commercial
that
debuted
on
May
28,
2009,
he
premiered
the
first
official
snippet
of
<i>Detox</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
50
Cent
and
Eminem
asserted
in
an
interview
on
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Entertainment
Television"
class="mw-redirect">BET</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/106_%26_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="106
&amp;
Park">106
&amp;
Park</a></i>
that
Dr.
Dre
had
around
a
dozen
songs
finished
for
<i>Detox</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
April
20,
2010,
&quot;Under
Pressure&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Jay-Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>
and
co-produced
with
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Storch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Storch">Scott
Storch</a>,
was
confirmed
by
Jimmy
Iovine
and
Dr.
Dre
during
an
interview
at
<a
href="/wiki/Fenway_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fenway
Park">Fenway
Park</a>
as
the
album's
first
single.<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
leaked
prior
to
its
intended
release
in
an
unmixed,
unmastered
form
without
a
chorus
on
June
16,
2010:<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
however,
critical
reaction
to
the
song
was
lukewarm,
and
Dr.
Dre
later
announced
in
an
interview
that
the
song,
along
with
any
other
previously
leaked
tracks
from
<i>Detox</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
recording
process,
would
not
appear
on
the
final
version
of
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
genuine
singles
â€“
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Kush_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kush
(song)">Kush</a>&quot;,
a
collaboration
with
Snoop
Dogg
and
fellow
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Akon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Akon">Akon</a>,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Need_a_Doctor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Need
a
Doctor">I
Need
a
Doctor</a>&quot;
with
Eminem
and
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Skylar_Grey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skylar
Grey">Skylar
Grey</a>
â€“
were
released
in
the
United
States
during
November
2010
and
February
2011
respectively:<sup
id="cite_ref-92"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-93"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
latter
achieved
international
chart
success,
reaching
number
four
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
and
later
being
certified
double
platinum
by
the
RIAA
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Australian
Recording
Industry
Association">Australian
Recording
Industry
Association</a>
(ARIA).<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_24-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-94"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
length
of
time
that
<i>Detox</i>
has
taken
to
record,
as
well
as
the
limited
amount
of
material
that
has
been
officially
released
or
leaked
from
the
recording
sessions,
has
given
it
considerable
notoriety
within
the
music
industry.<sup
id="cite_ref-dj-quik-detox_95-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-dj-quik-detox-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup>
Numerous
release
dates
(including
the
ones
mentioned
above)
have
been
given
for
the
album
over
the
years
since
it
was
first
announced,
although
none
of
them
have
transpired
to
be
genuine.<sup
id="cite_ref-hhwireddetox_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hhwireddetox-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-complex-detox_97-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-complex-detox-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup>
Several
musicians
closely
affiliated
with
Dr.
Dre,
including
Snoop
Dogg,
fellow
rappers
<a
href="/wiki/50_Cent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50
Cent">50
Cent</a>
and
Game
and
producer
<a
href="/wiki/DJ_Quik?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DJ
Quik">DJ
Quik</a>,
have
speculated
in
interviews
that
the
album
will
never
be
released,
due
to
Dr.
Dre's
business
and
entrepreneurial
ventures
having
interfered
with
recording
work,
as
well
as
causing
him
to
lose
motivation
to
record
new
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-hhwireddetox_96-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hhwireddetox-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-complex-detox_97-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-complex-detox-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Film_career">Film
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Film
career">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Dr.
Dre
made
his
first
on
screen
appearance
as
a
weapons
dealer
in
the
1996
bank
robbery
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Set_It_Off?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Set
It
Off">Set
It
Off</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-110"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
also
appeared
in
the
movies
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Wash_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Wash
(film)">The
Wash</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Training_Day?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Training
Day">Training
Day</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-musical_111-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-musical-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
song
of
his,
&quot;Bad
Intentions&quot;
(featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Knoc-Turn%27Al?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Knoc-Turn'Al"
class="mw-redirect">Knoc-Turn'Al</a>)
and
produced
by
Mahogany,
was
featured
on
<a
href="/wiki/The_Wash_(soundtrack)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Wash
(soundtrack)"><i>The
Wash</i>
soundtrack</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-112"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
also
appeared
on
two
other
songs
&quot;On
the
Blvd.&quot;
and
&quot;The
Wash&quot;
along
with
his
co-star
Snoop
Dogg.
In
February
2007
it
was
announced
that
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
would
produce
dark
comedies
and
horror
films
for
<a
href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Line
Cinema">New
Line
Cinema</a>-owned
company
Crucial
Films,
along
with
longtime
video
director
<a
href="/wiki/Phillip_Atwell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phillip
Atwell"
class="mw-redirect">Phillip
Atwell</a>.
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
announced
&quot;This
is
a
natural
switch
for
me,
since
I've
directed
a
lot
of
music
videos,
and
I
eventually
want
to
get
into
directing.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-113"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup>
Along
with
fellow
member
Ice
Cube,
Dr.
Dre
will
produce
a
biographical
film
about
N.W.A
tentatively
titled
<i>Straight
Outta
Compton</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-114"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Beats
By
Dr.
Dre
logo









</div>

</div>








<p>In
July
2008,
Dr.
Dre
released
his
brand
of
headphones,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Beats_by_Dr._Dre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beats
by
Dr.
Dre"
class="mw-redirect">Beats
by
Dr.
Dre</a></i>.
The
line
consists
of
Beats
Studio,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Headphones?qsrc=3044#Circumaural"
title="Headphones">circumaural</a>
headphone,
Beats
Tour,
an
in-ear
headphone,
Beats
Solo
&amp;
Solo
HD,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Supra-aural?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Supra-aural"
class="mw-redirect">supra-aural</a>
headphone,
Beats
Spin,
Heartbeats
by
<a
href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lady
Gaga">Lady
Gaga</a>,
also
an
in-ear
headphone,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_Combs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sean
Combs">Diddy</a>
Beats.<sup
id="cite_ref-115"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
is
also
planning
to
release
an
&quot;Aftermath
Cognac
and
vodka&quot;
at
around
the
same
time
he
releases
<i>Detox</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-116"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
the
2009
Fall
season,
HP
and
Dr.
Dre
teamed
up
to
release
Beats
By
Dr.
Dre
with
the
sale
of
all
HP
laptops
and
headsets.<sup
id="cite_ref-117"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup>
HP
and
Dr.
Dre
announced
the
deal
on
October
9,
2009,
at
a
press
event
in
<a
href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Santa
Monica,
California">Santa
Monica</a>,
California.
The
new
laptop,
known
as
HP
ENVY
15
Beats
limited
edition,
will
be
available
for
sale
October
22
and
be
priced
around
$2,299.
Besides
the
laptop,
the
PC
comes
with
Dr.
Dre's
signature
headphones.<sup
id="cite_ref-118"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
