<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_influences_and_style">Musical
influences
and
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
influences
and
style">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Dr.&nbsp;Dre
has
said
that
his
primary
instrument
in
the
studio
is
the
<a
href="/wiki/Music_Production_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
Production
Center">Akai
MPC3000</a>,
a
drum
machine
and
sampler,
and
that
he
often
uses
as
many
as
four
or
five
to
produce
a
single
recording.
He
cites
1970s
<a
href="/wiki/Funk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Funk">funk</a>
musicians
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/George_Clinton_(funk_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Clinton
(funk
musician)"
class="mw-redirect">George
Clinton</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Isaac_Hayes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Isaac
Hayes">Isaac
Hayes</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Curtis_Mayfield?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Curtis
Mayfield">Curtis
Mayfield</a>
as
his
primary
musical
influences.
Unlike
most
rap
producers,
he
tries
to
avoid
samples
as
much
as
possible,
preferring
to
have
studio
musicians
re-play
pieces
of
music
he
wants
to
use,
because
it
allows
him
more
flexibility
to
change
the
pieces
in
rhythm
and
tempo.<sup
id="cite_ref-scratch_2004_120-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-scratch_2004-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001
he
told
<i>Time</i>
magazine,
&quot;I
may
hear
something
I
like
on
an
old
record
that
may
inspire
me,
but
I'd
rather
use
musicians
to
re-create
the
sound
or
elaborate
on
it.
I
can
control
it
better.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-in_the_doctor.27s_house_121-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-in_the_doctor.27s_house-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
equipment
he
uses
include
the
<a
href="/wiki/E-mu_SP-1200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E-mu
SP-1200">E-mu
SP-1200</a>
drum
machine
and
other
keyboards
from
such
manufacturers
as
Korg,
Rhodes,
Wurlitzer,
Moog,
and
Roland.<sup
id="cite_ref-122"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
founding
Aftermath
Entertainment
in
1996,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
took
on
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Mel-Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mel-Man">Mel-Man</a>
as
a
co-producer,
and
his
music
took
on
a
more
synthesizer-based
sound,
using
fewer
vocal
samples
(as
he
had
used
on
&quot;Lil'
Ghetto
Boy&quot;
and
&quot;Let
Me
Ride&quot;
on
<i>The
Chronic</i>,
for
example).
Mel-Man
has
not
shared
co-production
credits
with
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
since
approximately
2002,
but
fellow
Aftermath
producer
Focus
has
credited
Mel-Man
as
a
key
architect
of
the
signature
Aftermath
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-123"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1999,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
started
working
with
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Elizondo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Elizondo">Mike
Elizondo</a>,
a
bassist,
guitarist,
and
keyboardist
who
has
also
produced,
written
and
played
on
records
for
female
singers
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Ann_Danielewski?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ann
Danielewski"
class="mw-redirect">Poe</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Fiona_Apple?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fiona
Apple">Fiona
Apple</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alanis
Morissette">Alanis
Morissette</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-124"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
past
few
years
Elizondo
has
since
worked
for
many
of
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
productions.<sup
id="cite_ref-shock_125-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-shock-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-songwriter_universe_126-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-songwriter_universe-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
also
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Scratch_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scratch
(magazine)">Scratch</a></i>
magazine
in
a
2004
interview
that
he
has
been
studying
piano
and
music
theory
formally,
and
that
a
major
goal
is
to
accumulate
enough
musical
theory
to
score
movies.
In
the
same
interview
he
stated
that
he
has
collaborated
with
famed
1960s
songwriter
<a
href="/wiki/Burt_Bacharach?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Burt
Bacharach">Burt
Bacharach</a>
by
sending
him
hip
hop
beats
to
play
over,
and
hopes
to
have
an
in-person
collaboration
with
him
in
the
future.<sup
id="cite_ref-scratch_2004_120-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-scratch_2004-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Work_ethic">Work
ethic</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Work
ethic">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Dr.&nbsp;Dre
has
stated
that
he
is
a
perfectionist
and
is
known
to
pressure
the
artists
with
whom
he
records
to
give
flawless
performances.<sup
id="cite_ref-scratch_2004_120-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-scratch_2004-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2006,
Snoop
Dogg
told
the
website
Dubcnn.com
that
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
had
made
new
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Bishop_Lamont?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bishop
Lamont">Bishop
Lamont</a>
re-record
a
single
bar
of
vocals
107&nbsp;times.<sup
id="cite_ref-127"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
has
also
stated
that
Eminem
is
a
fellow
perfectionist,
and
attributes
his
success
on
Aftermath
to
his
similar
work
ethic.<sup
id="cite_ref-scratch_2004_120-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-scratch_2004-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
gives
a
lot
of
input
into
the
delivery
of
the
vocals
and
will
stop
an
<a
href="/wiki/MC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MC"
class="mw-redirect">MC</a>
during
a
take
if
it
isn't
to
his
liking.<sup
id="cite_ref-128"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
he
does
give
<a
href="/wiki/MC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MC"
class="mw-redirect">MCs</a>
he
works
with
room
to
write
lyrics
without
too
much
instruction
unless
it
is
a
specifically
conceptual
record,
as
noted
by
<a
href="/wiki/Bishop_Lamont?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bishop
Lamont">Bishop
Lamont</a>
in
the
book
<i><a
href="/wiki/How_to_Rap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
to
Rap">How
to
Rap</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-129"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
consequence
of
his
perfectionism
is
that
some
artists
that
initially
sign
deals
with
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
Aftermath
label
never
release
albums.
In
2001,
Aftermath
released
the
soundtrack
to
the
movie
<i>The
Wash</i>,
featuring
a
number
of
Aftermath
acts
such
as
Shaunta,
Daks,
Joe
Beast
and
Toi.
To
date,
none
have
released
full-length
albums
on
Aftermath
and
have
apparently
ended
their
relationships
with
the
label
and
Dr.&nbsp;Dre.
Other
noteworthy
acts
to
leave
Aftermath
without
releasing
albums
include
<a
href="/wiki/King_Tee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="King
Tee">King
Tee</a>,
<i>2001</i>
vocalist
Hittman,
<a
href="/wiki/Joell_Ortiz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joell
Ortiz">Joell
Ortiz</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Raekwon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rakim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rakim">Rakim</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-source_2003_130-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-source_2003-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Collaborators_and_co-producers">Collaborators
and
co-producers</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17"
title="Edit
section:
Collaborators
and
co-producers">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Over
the
years,
word
of
other
collaborators
who
have
contributed
to
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
work
has
surfaced.
During
his
tenure
at
Death
Row
Records,
it
was
alleged
that
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
stepbrother
Warren
G
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tha_Dogg_Pound?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tha
Dogg
Pound">Tha
Dogg
Pound</a>
member
<a
href="/wiki/Daz_Dillinger?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Daz
Dillinger">Daz</a>
made
many
uncredited
contributions
to
songs
on
his
solo
album
<i>The
Chronic</i>
and
Snoop
Doggy
Dogg's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Doggystyle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doggystyle">Doggystyle</a></i>
(Daz
received
production
credits
on
Snoop's
similar-sounding,
albeit
less
successful
album
<i>Tha
Doggfather</i>
after
Young
left
Death
Row
Records).<sup
id="cite_ref-DPG-Eulogy_131-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-DPG-Eulogy-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>It
is
known
that
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Storch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Storch">Scott
Storch</a>,
who
has
since
gone
on
to
become
a
successful
producer
in
his
own
right,
contributed
to
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
second
album
<i>2001</i>;
Storch
is
credited
as
a
songwriter
on
several
songs
and
played
keyboards
on
several
tracks.
In
2006
he
told
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>:</p>








<blockquote>









<p>&quot;At
the
time,
I
saw
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
desperately
needed
something,&quot;
Storch
says.
&quot;He
needed
a
fuel
injection,
and
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
utilized
me
as
the
nitrous
oxide.
He
threw
me
into
the
mix,
and
I
sort
of
tapped
on
a
new
flavor
with
my
whole
piano
sound
and
the
strings
and
orchestration.
So
I'd
be
on
the
keyboards,
and
Mike
[Elizondo]
was
on
the
bass
guitar,
and
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
on
the
drum
machine&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-132"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<p>Current
collaborator
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Elizondo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Elizondo">Mike
Elizondo</a>,
when
speaking
about
his
work
with
Young,
describes
their
recording
process
as
a
collaborative
effort
involving
several
musicians.
In
2004
he
claimed
to
<i>Songwriter
Universe</i>
magazine
that
he
had
written
the
foundations
of
the
hit
Eminem
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Real_Slim_Shady?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Real
Slim
Shady">The
Real
Slim
Shady</a>&quot;,
stating,
&quot;I
initially
played
a
bass
line
on
the
song,
and
Dr.&nbsp;Dre,
Tommy
Coster
Jr.
and
I
built
the
track
from
there.
<a
href="/wiki/Eminem?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eminem">Eminem</a>
then
heard
the
track,
and
he
wrote
the
rap
to
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-songwriter_universe_126-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-songwriter_universe-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
account
is
essentially
confirmed
by
Eminem
in
his
book
<i>Angry
Blonde</i>,
stating
that
the
tune
for
the
song
was
composed
by
a
studio
bassist
and
keyboardist
while
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
out
of
the
studio
but
Young
later
programmed
the
song's
beat
after
returning.<sup
id="cite_ref-133"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
group
of
disgruntled
former
associates
of
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
complained
that
they
had
not
received
their
full
due
for
work
on
the
label
in
the
September
2003
issue
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Source
(magazine)">The
Source</a></i>.
A
producer
named
Neff-U
claimed
to
have
produced
the
songs
&quot;Say
What
You
Say&quot;
and
&quot;My
Dad's
Gone
Crazy&quot;
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Eminem_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Eminem
Show">The
Eminem
Show</a></i>,
the
songs
&quot;If
I
Can't&quot;
and
&quot;Back
Down&quot;
on
50
Cent's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_Rich_or_Die_Tryin%27_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
Rich
or
Die
Tryin'
(album)">Get
Rich
or
Die
Tryin'</a></i>,
and
the
beat
featured
on
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
commercial
for
<a
href="/wiki/Coors_Brewing_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coors
Brewing
Company">Coors
beer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-source_2003_130-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-source_2003-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Although
Young
studies
piano
and
musical
theory,
he
serves
as
more
of
a
<a
href="/wiki/Conductor_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Conductor
(music)"
class="mw-redirect">conductor</a>
than
a
musician
himself,
as
Josh
Tyrangiel
of
<i>TIME</i>
magazine
has
noted:</p>








<blockquote>









<p>Every
Dre
track
begins
the
same
way,
with
Dre
behind
a
drum
machine
in
a
room
full
of
trusted
musicians.
(They
carry
beepers.
When
he
wants
to
work,
they
work.)
He'll
program
a
beat,
then
ask
the
musicians
to
play
along;
when
Dre
hears
something
he
likes,
he
isolates
the
player
and
tells
him
how
to
refine
the
sound.
&quot;My
greatest
talent,&quot;
Dre
says,
&quot;is
knowing
exactly
what
I
want
to
hear.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-in_the_doctor.27s_house_121-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-in_the_doctor.27s_house-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<p>Although
Snoop
Dogg
retains
working
relationships
with
Warren
G
and
Daz,
who
are
alleged
to
be
uncredited
contributors
on
the
hit
albums
<i>The
Chronic</i>
and
<i>Doggystyle</i>,
he
states
that
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
is
capable
of
making
beats
without
the
help
of
collaborators,
and
that
he
is
responsible
for
the
success
of
his
numerous
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-134"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
prominent
studio
collaborators,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Storch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Storch">Scott
Storch</a>,
Elizondo,
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Batson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Batson">Mark
Batson</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Dawaun_Parker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dawaun
Parker">Dawaun
Parker</a>,
have
shared
co-writing,
instrumental,
and
more
recently
co-production
credits
on
the
songs
where
he
is
credited
as
the
producer.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Ghostwriters">Ghostwriters</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"
title="Edit
section:
Ghostwriters">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>It
is
acknowledged
that
most
of
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
raps
are
written
for
him
by
others,
though
he
retains
ultimate
control
over
his
lyrics
and
the
themes
of
his
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC_135-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
Aftermath
producer
Mahogany
told
<i>Scratch</i>:
&quot;It's
like
a
class
room
in
[the
booth].
He'll
have
three
writers
in
there.
They'll
bring
in
something,
he'll
recite
it,
then
he'll
say.
'Change
this
line,
change
this
word,'
like
he's
grading
papers.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-scratch_2006_136-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-scratch_2006-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
seen
in
the
credits
for
tracks
Young
has
appeared
on,
there
are
often
multiple
people
who
contribute
to
his
songs
(although
often
in
hip
hop
many
people
are
officially
credited
as
a
writer
for
a
song,
even
the
producer).</p>








<p>In
the
book
<i><a
href="/wiki/How_to_Rap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="How
to
Rap">How
to
Rap</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/RBX?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RBX">RBX</a>
explains
that
writing
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Chronic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chronic">The
Chronic</a></i>
was
a
&quot;team
effort&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC_135-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
details
how
he
<a
href="/wiki/Ghostwriter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ghostwriter">ghostwrote</a>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_Me_Ride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
Me
Ride">Let
Me
Ride</a>&quot;
for
Dre.<sup
id="cite_ref-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC_135-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
regard
to
ghostwriting
lyrics
he
says,
&quot;Dre
doesn't
profess
to
be
no
super-duper
rap
dude
â€“
Dre
is
a
super-duper
producer&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC_135-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Edwards.2C_Paul_2009.2C_p_MC-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
a
member
of
N.W.A,
The
D.O.C.
wrote
lyrics
for
him
while
he
stuck
with
producing.<sup
id="cite_ref-doc_formula_20-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-doc_formula-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
New
York
City
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Jay-Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>
ghostwrote
lyrics
for
the
single
&quot;Still
D.R.E.&quot;
from
Dr.&nbsp;Dre's
album
<i>2001</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-changes_2001_42-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-changes_2001-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Personal_life">Personal
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19"
title="Edit
section:
Personal
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Relationships_and_family">Relationships
and
family</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20"
title="Edit
section:
Relationships
and
family">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Dr.
Dre's
eldest
son
is
named
Curtis
Young.
When
Curtis
Young
was
born,
Greene
was
16,
and
Dr.
Dre
was
17.
Curtis
Young
is
an
aspiring
rapper
who
goes
by
the
rap
moniker
&quot;Hood
Surgeon&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-137"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1988,
Dr.
Dre
had
his
second
son,
Andre
Young
Jr.,
with
Jenita
Porter.
Porter
sued
Dr.
Dre
in
1990
in
Orange
County
Superior
Court
seeking
$5,000
of
child
support
per
month.<sup
id="cite_ref-Andre_Jr_138-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Andre_Jr-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup>
From
1990
to
1996,
Dr.
Dre
dated
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Michel%27le?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michel'le">Michel'le</a>,
who
frequently
contributed
vocals
to
Death
Row
Records
albums.
In
1991,
the
couple
had
a
son,
Marcel.<sup
id="cite_ref-139"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1996,
Dr.
Dre
married
Nicole
Threatt,
the
ex-wife
of
<a
href="/wiki/NBA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NBA"
class="mw-redirect">NBA</a>
player
<a
href="/wiki/Sedale_Threatt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sedale
Threatt">Sedale
Threatt</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-140"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
have
two
children
together:
a
son
named
Truth
(born
1997)
and
a
daughter
named
Truly
(born
2001).<sup
id="cite_ref-141"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
August
23,
2008,
Young's
second
son,
Andre
Young
Jr.,
died
at
the
age
of
20
at
his
mother's
<a
href="/wiki/Woodland_Hills,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woodland
Hills,
California"
class="mw-redirect">Woodland
Hills</a>
home.<sup
id="cite_ref-Andre_Jr_138-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Andre_Jr-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
coroner
determined
that
he
died
from
an
overdose
of
<a
href="/wiki/Heroin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heroin">heroin</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Morphine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Morphine">morphine</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-142"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Income">Income</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21"
title="Edit
section:
Income">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2001,
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
earned
a
total
of
about
US$52&nbsp;million
from
selling
part
of
his
share
of
Aftermath
Entertainment
to
<a
href="/wiki/Interscope_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Interscope
Records">Interscope
Records</a>
and
his
production
of
such
hit
songs
that
year
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Family_Affair_(Mary_J._Blige_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Family
Affair
(Mary
J.
Blige
song)">Family
Affair</a>&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mary
J.
Blige">Mary
J.
Blige</a>.
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
magazine
thus
named
him
the
second
highest-paid
artist
of
the
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-wealth_2001_50-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wealth_2001-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dr.&nbsp;Dre
was
ranked
44th
in
2004
from
earnings
of
$11.4&nbsp;million,
primarily
from
production
royalties
from
such
projects
as
albums
from
<a
href="/wiki/G-Unit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/D12?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="D12">D12</a>
and
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rich_Girl_(Gwen_Stefani_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rich
Girl
(Gwen
Stefani
song)">Rich
Girl</a>&quot;
by
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gwen
Stefani">Gwen
Stefani</a>
and
rapper
<a
href="/wiki/Eve_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eve
(entertainer)">Eve</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-wealth_2004_143-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wealth_2004-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup>
Forbes
estimated
his
net
worth
at
US$270
million
in
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-144"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
same
publication
later
reported
that,
he
acquired
US$110&nbsp;million
via
his
various
endeavors
in
2012,
making
him
the
highestâ€“paid
artist
of
the
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-145"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards
and
nominations</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Dr._Dre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23"
title="Edit
section:
Awards
and
nominations">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Dr.
Dre
has
won
six
Grammy
Awards.
Three
of
them
are
for
his
production
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-146"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-147"

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Dr._Dre&page=1&ac=24&qid=62AC393B1931B432432A480B27AE6DD4&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
